A little fun fact in case most people kinda noticed it, Yokohama Japan (according to a brief google search) runs on 50hz electric instead of 60hz like the US does. Most electricity is AC (alternating current) that turns on and off so quickly you donâ€™t notice it, itâ€™s more efficient that DC (direct current) which is used in low voltage electronics. Hz is hertz that means rotations for 60, so 50hz is 50 times per second and 60hz would be 60. This means that if you are used to an area that has 60hz you may notice the quick flickering of lights in areas that have 50hz typically overseas.

14:36  I don't either, but it's probably easier to understand than what I'm used to.  Honestly, for a second I was thinking about how cool it would be to go to a card game shop in Japan and get Yu-Gi-Oh cards, then I remembered that doing so would be near worthless because Komoney doesn't let us in the TCG use OCG cards.  Their reason. They've never directly said this, because of legal reasons or whatever, but it's very clearly because letting us use OCG cards would destroy the second hand market of TCG cards.  Long story short, the OCG prints cards in more rarities making them more affordable for people with less money. The TCG doesn't.  Well, not quite. They recently added a new rarity that does help a bit, and so far it seems to be working decently well.  Unchained soul Lord of Yama would've probably been a $40-ish card, but the it's closer to $20 because anyone who wants max rarity can pick up a quarter century secret are for around $130-$160.  It's not a great example, but it's the best example that I have. Not much else in DUNE was that influential. We'll probably (maybe) have a better reference point moving into AGOV.

I went to Japan recently, can highly recommend, it has something for everyone, provided you can walk a lot and take trains a lot. Knowing some Japanese can be really helpful, everyone going should at least learn Katakana and get an offline OCR translator on their phone imo.  My trip was very unlike Alpharad's, I did visit plenty of the places he mentioned but bought less than $50 on merch over my whole trip (approx. 25 days).  I visited Hiroshima, Kyoto, Nara, and main based in Tokyo.  Climbed Mt. Fuji to the real summit and down in a day (there's a real summit and a kind of summit that's actually not that many people stop at).  Visited plenty of anime stuff.  Even though I'm vegan with the use of the happy cow app/site I had no trouble finding fully vegan places in Tokyo nearby at almost all times, and in every city there were at least vegan options. This honestly surprised me after how many horror stories I've heard, and yes let's more foods did have dairy/egg in e.g. melon pan.

Everyone ask me "how much money you need to have when you're going to Japan" and the only answer is "normally around 3k USD including airplane ticket for 3 weeks without being obliged to save on each step, but if you're weeb - credit card debt is the limit". There is so much thing to "waste" money on like sitting 8 hours in arcade and destroying locals in Tekken or Initial D Arcade, buying gatcha, console games, gaming consoles (fun fact, new PS5 in Japan even after paying import taxes is 2x times cheaper than in my country), anime figurines, mangas, shady DVD's from basement stores - you name it. I am intentionaly not mentioning eating, because main problem here is stomach capacity not money, because food for me were extremely cheap in Japan while I know that other nations complains about prices of japanese food, but in my country cheapest meal option, in cheapest bar not even a restaurant cost around 15USD while durning 3 weeks in Japan I can count on fingers of 1 hand how many times I ate meal in restaurant for more than 10USD and usually that was options like kobe beef or fancy japanese burgers. So when you're going to Japan and you want to respect your hard earned money first rule - DON'T BE WEEB - or you will be that guy on airport for return flight that have 6 suitcases only for himself.
